<ul><li>As phonemes, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/iː/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/uː/</span> occur only in the words <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">spieël</i></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/spiːl/</span> 'mirror' and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">koeël</i></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/kuːl/</span> 'bullet', which used to be pronounced with sequences <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i.ə/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/u.ə/</span>, respectively. In other cases, <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">iː</a>&#93;</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">uː</a>&#93;</span> occur as allophones of, respectively, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/u/</span> before <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/y/</span> is phonetically long <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Close_front_rounded_vowel" title="Close front rounded vowel">yː</a>&#93;</span> before <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDonaldson19935–6_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDonaldson19935–6-87">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/əː/</span> is always stressed and occurs only in the word <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">wîe</i></i> 'wedges'.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The closest unrounded counterparts of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/œ, œː/</span> are central <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ə, əː/</span>, rather than front <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛ, ɛː/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/œː, ɔː/</span> occur only in a few words.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>As a phoneme, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/æ/</span> occurs as an allophone of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛ/</span> before <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k, χ, l, r/</span>, though this occurs primarily dialectally, most commonly in the former <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Transvaal Province">Transvaal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_State_(South_African_province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Free State (South African province)">Free State</a> provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-don37_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-don37-91">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<ul><li>All <a href="/wiki/Obstruent" title="Obstruent">obstruents</a> at the ends of words are <a href="/wiki/Final-obstruent_devoicing" title="Final-obstruent devoicing">devoiced</a>, so that e.g. a final <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/d/</span> is realized as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[t]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDonaldson199313–15_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDonaldson199313–15-95">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɡ, dʒ, z/</span> occur only in loanwords. <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ɡ]</span> is also an allophone of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/χ/</span> in some environments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDonaldson199313–14,_20–22_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDonaldson199313–14,_20–22-96">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/χ/</span> is most often uvular <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">χ</a> ~ <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_trill" title="Voiceless uvular trill">ʀ̥</a>]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wells_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wells-98">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Velar <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">x</a>&#93;</span> occurs only in some speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-wells_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wells-98">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span> is usually an alveolar trill <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" class="mw-redirect" title="Alveolar trill">r</a>&#93;</span> or tap <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Alveolar_tap" class="mw-redirect" title="Alveolar tap">ɾ</a>&#93;</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELass1987117_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELass1987117-100">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In some parts of the former <a href="/wiki/Cape_Province" title="Cape Province">Cape Province</a>, it is realized uvularly, either as a trill <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Uvular_trill" title="Uvular trill">ʀ</a>&#93;</span> or a fricative <span class="IPA nowrap" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_uvular_fricative" title="Voiced uvular fricative">ʁ</a>&#93;</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDonaldson199315_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDonaldson199315-101">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><br />
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Dialects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg/220px-Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg/330px-Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg/440px-Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Graham_Maclachlan_-_Gevaar_Slagysters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A warning sign in Afrikaans: <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Gevaar Slagysters</i></i> or "Danger, Bear Traps".</div></div></div>
<p>Following early dialectal studies of Afrikaans, it was theorised that three main historical dialects probably existed after the Great Trek in the 1830s. These dialects are the Northern Cape, Western Cape, and Eastern Cape dialects.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Northern Cape dialect may have resulted from contact between Dutch settlers and the <a href="/wiki/Khoi-Khoi" class="mw-redirect" title="Khoi-Khoi">Khoi-Khoi</a> people between the Great Karoo and the Kunene, and Eastern Cape dialect between the Dutch and the Xhosa. Remnants of these dialects still remain in present-day Afrikaans, although the standardising effect of Standard Afrikaans has contributed to a great levelling of differences in modern times.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-103">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>There is also a prison <a href="/wiki/Cant_(language)" title="Cant (language)">cant</a>, known as <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">soebela</i> or <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sombela</i>, which is based on Afrikaans, yet heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>. This language is used as a secret language in prison and is taught to initiates.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-103">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kaapse_Afrikaans"><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Kaapse Afrikaans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The term <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i></i> ("Cape Afrikaans") is sometimes erroneously used to refer to the entire Western Cape dialect; it is more commonly used for a particular sociolect spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Peninsula" title="Cape Peninsula">Cape Peninsula</a> of South Africa. <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i> was once spoken by all population groups. However, it became increasingly restricted to the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Coloured" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Coloured">Cape Coloured</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a> and environs. Kaapse Afrikaans is still understood by the large majority of native Afrikaans speakers in South Africa.
</p><p><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i> preserves some features more similar to Dutch than to Afrikaans.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The 1st person singular pronoun <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">ik</i></i> as in Dutch as opposed to Afrikaans <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ek</i></i></li>
<li>The diminutive endings <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">-tje</i></i>, pronounced as in Dutch and not as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ki/</span> as in Afrikaans.</li>
<li>The use of the form <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">seg</i></i> (compare Dutch <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">zegt</i></i>) as opposed to Afrikaans <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sê</i></i></li></ul>
<p><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i> has some other features not typically found in Afrikaans.
</p>
<ul><li>The pronunciation of <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">j</i></i>, normally <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/j/</span> as in Dutch is often a <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/dz/</span>. This is the strongest feature of <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i>.</li>
<li>The insertion of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/j/</span> after <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/s/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k/</span> when followed by <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/e/</span>, e.g. <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kjen</i></i> as opposed to Standard Afrikaans <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ken</i></i>.</li></ul>
<p><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i> is also characterised by much <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">code-switching</a> between <a href="/wiki/South_African_English" title="South African English">English</a> and Afrikaans, especially in the inner-city and lower socio-economic status areas of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>.
</p><p>An example of characteristic <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i>:
</p>
<dl><dd><a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">En ik zeg (tegen) jullie: wat zoeken jullie hier bij mij? Ik zoek jullie niet! Nee, ga nu weg!</i></dd>
<dd><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Kaapse Afrikaans</i>: | <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">En ik seg ve' djille, wat soek djille hie' by my? Ik soek'ie ve' djille nie! Nei, gaat nou weg!</i></dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Afrikaans_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrikaans language">Afrikaans</a>: <i lang="af">En ek sê vir julle, wat soek julle hier by my? Ek soek julle nie! Nee, gaan nou weg!</i></dd>
<dd>English (literal): | And I say to you, what seek you here by me? I seek you not! No, go now away!</dd>
<dd>English: And I'm telling you, what are you looking for here? I'm not looking for you! No, go away now!</dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oranjerivierafrikaans"><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Oranjerivierafrikaans</i></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Oranjerivierafrikaans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The term <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Oranjerivierafrikaans</i></i> ("Afrikaans of the Orange River") is sometimes erroneously used to refer to the Northern Cape dialect; it is more commonly used for the regional peculiarities of standard Afrikaans spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Upington" title="Upington">Upington</a>/<a href="/w/index.php?title=Orange_River_wine_district&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Orange River wine district (page does not exist)">Orange River wine district</a> of South Africa.
</p><p>Some of the characteristics of <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Oranjerivierafrikaans</i> are the plural form <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">-goed</i></i> (<i>Ma-<i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">goed</i></i>, <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">meneergoed</i></i>), variant pronunciation such as in <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kjerk</i></i> ("Church") and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">gjeld</i></i> ("money") and the ending <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">-se</i></i>, which indicates possession.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expatriate_geolect">Expatriate geolect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Expatriate geolect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although Afrikaans is mainly spoken in South Africa and Namibia, smaller Afrikaans-speaking populations live in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Australia, <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, Canada, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, New Zealand, <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a>, the UAE, the United Kingdom, Republic of Ireland, the US, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-e19_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e19-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Most Afrikaans-speaking people living outside Africa are emigrants and their descendants. Because of <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">emigration</a> and migrant labour, more than 100,000 Afrikaans speakers may live in the United Kingdom.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences_on_Afrikaans_from_other_languages">Influences on Afrikaans from other languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Influences on Afrikaans from other languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malay">Malay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Malay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to the early settlement of a <a href="/wiki/Cape_Malay" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Malay">Cape Malay</a> community in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, who are now known as <a href="/wiki/Coloured" class="mw-redirect" title="Coloured">Coloureds</a>, numerous <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Malay_language#Classical_Malay" title="History of the Malay language">Classical Malay</a> words were brought into Afrikaans. Some of these words entered Dutch via people arriving from, what is now known as, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> as part of their colonial heritage. Malay words in Afrikaans include:<sup id="cite_ref-safariafrica.co.za_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-safariafrica.co.za-106">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">baie</i></b>, which means 'very'/'much'/'many' (from <i><i lang="id" title="Indonesian language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/banyak" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:banyak">banyak</a></i></i>) is a very commonly used Afrikaans word, different from its Dutch equivalent <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">veel</i></i> or <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">erg</i></i>.</li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">baadjie</i></b>, Afrikaans for <a href="/wiki/Jacket" title="Jacket">jacket</a>, where Dutch would use <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">jas</i></i> or <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">vest</i></i>. The word <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">baadje</i></i> in Dutch is now considered archaic and only used in written, literary texts.</li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">piesang</i></b>, which means <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>. This is different from the common Dutch word <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">banaan</i></i>. The Indonesian word <i><i lang="id" title="Indonesian language text">pisang</i></i> is also used in Dutch, though usage is less common.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese">Portuguese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Portuguese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some words originally came from Portuguese such as <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sambreel</i></i> ("umbrella") from the Portuguese <i><i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">sombreiro</i></i>, <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kraal</i></i> ("pen/cattle enclosure") from the Portuguese <i><i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">curral</i></i>, and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">mielie</i></i> ("corn", from <i><i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">milho</i></i>). These words have become common in South Africa to an extent of being used in many other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">South African languages</a>. Some of these words also exist in Dutch, like <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">sambreel</i></i> "parasol",<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> though usage is less common and meanings can slightly differ.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Khoisan_languages">Khoisan languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Khoisan languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">dagga</i></b>, meaning cannabis<sup id="cite_ref-safariafrica.co.za_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-safariafrica.co.za-106">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">geitjie</i></b>, meaning lizard, diminutive adapted from <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Khoekhoe">Khoekhoe</a> word<sup id="cite_ref-austin_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-austin-108">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">gogga</i></b>, meaning insect, from the <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">Khoisan</a> <i>xo-xo</i></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">karos</i></b>, blanket of animal hides</li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kierie</i></b> walking stick from <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Khoekhoe">Khoekhoe</a><sup id="cite_ref-austin_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-austin-108">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Some of these words also exist in Dutch, though with a more specific meaning: <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">assegaai</i></i> for example means "South-African tribal javelin"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">karos</i></i> means "South-African tribal blanket of animal hides".<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bantu_languages">Bantu languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Bantu languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Loanwords from <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu languages</a> in Afrikaans include the names of indigenous birds, such as <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">mahem</i></i> and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sakaboela</i></i>, and indigenous plants, such as <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">maroela</i></i> and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">tamboekie(gras)</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Potgieter_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Potgieter-110">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">fundi</i></b>, from the <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> word <i><i lang="zu" title="Zulu language text">umfundi</i></i> meaning "scholar" or "student",<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> but used to mean someone who is a student/expert on a certain subject, i.e. <i>He is a language <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">fundi</i></i>.</li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">lobola</i></b>, meaning bride price, from (and referring to) <i><a href="/wiki/Lobolo" title="Lobolo">lobolo</a></i> of the <a href="/wiki/Nguni_languages" title="Nguni languages">Nguni languages</a><sup id="cite_ref-Ngcongwane_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ngcongwane-112">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">mahem</i></b>, the <a href="/wiki/Grey_crowned_crane" title="Grey crowned crane">grey crowned crane</a>, known in Latin as <i>Balearica regulorum</i></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">maroela</i></b>, medium-sized <a href="/wiki/Dioecy" title="Dioecy">dioecious</a> tree known in Latin as <i><a href="/wiki/Sclerocarya_birrea" title="Sclerocarya birrea">Sclerocarya birrea</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">tamboekiegras</i></b>, species of thatching grass known as <a href="/wiki/Hyparrhenia" title="Hyparrhenia">Hyparrhenia</a><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">tambotie</i></b>, deciduous tree also known by its <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> name, <i><a href="/wiki/Spirostachys_africana" title="Spirostachys africana">Spirostachys africana</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">tjaila</i> / <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">tjailatyd</i></b>, an adaption of the word <i><i lang="zu" title="Zulu language text">chaile</i></i>, meaning "to go home" or "to knock off".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French">French</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: French">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The revoking of the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Nantes" title="Edict of Nantes">Edict of Nantes</a> on the 22nd of October 1685 was a milestone in the history of <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, for it marked the beginning of the great <a href="/wiki/Huguenots" title="Huguenots">Huguenot</a> exodus from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. It is estimated that between 250,000 and 300,000 Protestants left France between 1685 and 1700; out of these, according to <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Michel_le_Tellier,_Marquis_de_Louvois" title="François-Michel le Tellier, Marquis de Louvois">Louvois</a>, 100,000 had received military training. A measure of the calibre of these immigrants and of their acceptance by host countries (in particular South Africa) is given by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Vollam_Morton" title="Henry Vollam Morton">H.V. Morton</a> in his book: In search of South Africa (London, 1948). The Huguenots were responsible for a great linguistic contribution to Afrikaans, particularly in terms of military terminology as many of them fought on the battlefields during the wars of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Trek" title="Great Trek">Great Trek</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Orthography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are many parallels between the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_orthography" title="Dutch orthography">Dutch orthography</a> conventions and those used for Afrikaans. There are 26 letters.
</p><p>In Afrikaans, many consonants are dropped from the earlier Dutch spelling. For example, <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">slechts</i></i> ('only') in Dutch becomes <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">slegs</i></i> in Afrikaans. Also, Afrikaans and some Dutch dialects make no distinction between <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/s/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span>, having merged the latter into the former; while the word for "south" is written <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">zuid</i></i> in Dutch, it is spelled <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">suid</i></i> in Afrikaans (as well as dialectal Dutch writings) to represent this merger. Similarly, the Dutch digraph <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text"><a href="/wiki/IJ_(digraph)" title="IJ (digraph)">ĳ</a></i></i>, normally pronounced as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/əi/</span>, is written as <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">y</i></i>, except where it replaces the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Affix" title="Affix">suffix</a> <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">–lijk</i></i> which is pronounced as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/lœk/</span> or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/lik/</span>, as in <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">waarschijnlijk</i> &gt; <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">waarskynlik</i></i>.
</p><p>Another difference is the indefinite article, <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'n</i></i> in Afrikaans and <i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">een</i> in Dutch. "A book" is <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'n boek</i></i> in Afrikaans, whereas it is either <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">een boek</i></i> or <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">'n boek</i></i> in Dutch. This <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'n</i></i> is usually pronounced as just a <a href="/wiki/Weak_vowel" class="mw-redirect" title="Weak vowel">weak vowel</a>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ə]</span>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Diminutive" title="Diminutive">diminutive</a> suffix in Afrikaans is <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">-tjie</i></i>, whereas in Dutch it is <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">-tje</i></i>, hence a "bit" is <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">bie<b>tjie</b></i> in Afrikaans and <i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">bee<b>tje</b></i> in Dutch.
</p><p>The letters <i>c</i>, <i>q</i>, <i>x</i>, and <i>z</i> occur almost exclusively in borrowings from French, English, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>. This is usually because words that had <i>c</i> and <i>ch</i> in the original Dutch are spelled with <i>k</i> and <i>g</i>, respectively, in Afrikaans. Similarly original <i>qu</i> and <i>x</i> are spelt <i>kw</i> and <i>ks</i>, respectively. For example, <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ekwatoriaal</i></i> instead of <i>equatoriaal</i>, and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ekskuus</i></i> instead of <i>excuus</i>.
</p><p>The vowels with diacritics in non-loanword Afrikaans are: <i>á</i>, <i>é</i>, <i>è</i>, <i>ê</i>, <i>ë</i>, <i>í</i>, <i>î</i>, <i>ï</i>, <i>ó</i>, <i>ô</i>, <i>ö</i>, <i>ú</i>, <i>û</i>, <i>ü</i>, <i>ý</i>. Diacritics are ignored when alphabetising, though they are still important, even when typing the diacritic forms may be difficult. For example, <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">geëet</i></i> instead of the 3 e's alongside each other: <i>*<i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">geeet</i></i>, which can never occur in Afrikaans, or <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sê</i></i>, which translates to "say", whereas <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">se</i></i> is a possessive form.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_apostrophes">Initial apostrophes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Initial apostrophes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A few short words in Afrikaans take initial apostrophes. In modern Afrikaans, these words are always written in lower case (except if the entire line is uppercase), and if they occur at the beginning of a sentence, the next word is capitalised. Three examples of such apostrophed words are <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'k, 't, 'n</i></i>. The last (the indefinite article) is the only apostrophed word that is common in modern written Afrikaans, since the other examples are shortened versions of other words (<i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ek</i></i> and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">het</i></i>, respectively) and are rarely found outside of a poetic context.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Here are a few examples:
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Apostrophed version
</th>
<th>Usual version
</th>
<th>Translation
</th>
<th>Notes
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'k 't Dit gesê</i>
</td>
<td><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Ek het dit gesê</i>
</td>
<td>I said it
</td>
<td>Uncommon, more common: <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Ek't dit gesê</i></i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'t Jy dit geëet?</i>
</td>
<td><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Het jy dit geëet?</i>
</td>
<td>Did you eat it?
</td>
<td>Extremely uncommon
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'n Man loop daar</i>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>A man walks there
</td>
<td>Standard Afrikaans pronounces <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'n</i></i> as a <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a> vowel.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The apostrophe and the following letter are regarded as two separate characters, and are never written using a single glyph, although a single character variant of the indefinite article appears in Unicode, <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ŉ</i>.
</p>

<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛ/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɪə/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ə/</span>
</td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">bed</i></i> ('bed'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛ/</span>), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ete</i></i> ('meal'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɪə/</span>), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">se</i></i> (<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ə/</span>; indicates possession, for example <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Johan se boom</i></i>, meaning 'John's tree')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>è</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">nè</i></i> ('yes?', 'right?'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">dè</i></i> ('here, take this!' or '[this is] yours!')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ê</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/eː/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛː/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/æ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sê</i></i> ('to say'). Represents <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛː/</span> word-finally, represents <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/æ/</span> before <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/x/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/l/</span>, or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ë</td>
<td>-
</td>
<td>Diaeresis indicates the start of new syllable, thus <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ë</i></i>, <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ëe</i></i> and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ëi</i></i> are pronounced like 'e', 'ee' and 'ei', respectively
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ee</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɪə/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">weet</i></i> ('to know'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">een</i></i> ('one')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>eeu</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/iːu/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sneeu</i></i> ('snow'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">eeu</i></i> ('century')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ei</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛːi/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">lei</i></i> ('to lead')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>eu</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɪø/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">seun</i></i> ('son' or 'lad')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>f</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/f/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">fiets</i></i> ('bicycle')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>g</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/x/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɡ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">goed</i></i> ('good'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/x/</span>), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">erger</i></i> ('worse'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɡ/</span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>gh</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɡ/</span>
</td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">gholf</i></i> ('golf'). Used for <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɡ/</span> when it is not an allophone of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/x/</span>; found only in borrowed words
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>h</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɦ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">hael</i></i> ('hail'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">hond</i></i> ('dog')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>i</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ə/</span>
</td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kind</i></i> ('child'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ə/</span>), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ink</i></i> ('ink'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ə/</span>), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">krisis</i></i> ('crisis'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/</span> for first 'i' and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ə/</span> for second 'i'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">elektrisiteit</i></i> ('electricity'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/</span> for first and second 'i'; third 'i' is part of diphthong 'ei')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>î</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/əː/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">wîe</i></i> (plural of <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">wig</i></i>; 'wedges' or 'quoins')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ï</td>
<td>-
</td>
<td>Found in words such as <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">beïnvloed</i></i> ('to influence'). The diaeresis indicates the start of new syllable, thus <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ï</i></i> and <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ïe</i></i> are pronounced like 'i' and 'ie' respectively
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ie</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">iets</i></i> ('something')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>j</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/j/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">jonk</i></i> ('young')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>k</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kat</i></i> ('cat'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kan</i></i> ('can' (verb) or 'jug')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>l</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/l/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">lag</i></i> ('laugh')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>m</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/m/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">man</i></i> ('man')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>n</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/n/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">nael</i></i> ('nail')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ng</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ŋ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sing</i></i> ('to sing')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>o</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɔ/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʊə/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">op</i></i> ('on' or 'up'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɔ/</span>), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">bote</i></i> ('boats'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʊə/</span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ô</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɔː/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">môre</i></i> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/morrow" class="extiw" title="wikt:morrow">'tomorrow'</a>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ö</td>
<td>-
</td>
<td>Found in words such as <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">mikroörganisme</i></i> ('micro-organism'). The diaeresis indicates the start of new syllable, thus <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ö</i></i> is pronounced the same as 'o'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>oe</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/u/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">boek</i></i> ('book'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">koel</i></i> ('cool')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>oei</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ui/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">koei</i></i> ('cow')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>oo</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʊə/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">oor</i></i> ('ear' or 'over')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ooi</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/oːi/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">mooi</i></i> ('pretty', 'beautiful'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">nooi</i></i> ('saying for little girl' or 'invitation')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ou</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɵu/</span>
</td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">oupa</i></i> ('grandpa', 'grandfather'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">koud</i></i> ('cold'). Sometimes spelled <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ouw</i></i> in loanwords and surnames, for example <i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Louw</i>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>p</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/p/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">pot</i></i> ('pot'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">pers</i></i> ('purple' — or 'press' indicating the news media)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>q</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k/</span>
</td>
<td>Found only in foreign words with original spelling maintained; typically <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">k</i></i> is used instead
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>r</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">rooi</i></i> ('red')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>s</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/s/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʃ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ses</i></i> ('six'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">stem</i></i> ('voice' or 'vote'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">posisie</i></i> ('position', <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span> for first 's', <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/s/</span> for second 's'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">rasioneel</i></i> ('rational', <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʃ/</span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>sj</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʃ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sjaal</i></i> ('shawl'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">sjokolade</i></i> ('chocolate')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>t</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʃ/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">tafel</i></i> ('table'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">aktuaris</i></i> ('actuary'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʃ/</span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>tj</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/tʃ/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/k/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">tjank</i></i> ('whine like a dog' or 'to cry incessantly'). The former pronunciation occurs at the beginning of a word and the latter in <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text"><a href="/wiki/List_of_diminutives_by_language#Afrikaans" title="List of diminutives by language">"-tjie"</a></i></i>, where it can also represent <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/c/</span> in some accents
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>u</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/œ/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/yː/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kus</i></i> ('coast' or 'kiss'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">skadu</i></i> ('shade'). The latter pronunciation is rare and most commonly found as the word <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">u</i></i> (formal 'you')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>û</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/œː/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">brûe</i></i> ('bridges')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ü</td>
<td>-
</td>
<td>Found in words such as <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">reünie</i></i> ('reunion'). The diaeresis indicates the start of a new syllable, thus <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">ü</i></i> is pronounced the same <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">u</i></i>, except when found in proper nouns and surnames from German, like <i lang="de" title="German language text">Müller</i>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ui</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/œj/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">uit</i></i> ('out')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>uu</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/yː/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">uur</i></i> ('hour')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>v</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/f/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">vis</i></i> ('fish'), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">vir</i></i> ('for')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>w</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/v/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/w/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">water</i></i> ('water'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/v/</span>); represents <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/w/</span> after consonants; an example: <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">kwassie</i></i> ('brush'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/w/</span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>x</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ks/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">xifoïed</i></i> ('xiphoid'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span>), <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">x-straal</i></i> ('x-ray'; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ks/</span>).
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>y</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ɛi/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">byt</i></i> ('bite')
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>z</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span></td>
<td><i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Zoeloe</i></i> ('Zulu'). Found only in <a href="/wiki/Onomatopoeia" title="Onomatopoeia">onomatopoeia</a> and loanwords
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Afrikaans_phrases">Afrikaans phrases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Afrikaans phrases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA"><img alt="[]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" decoding="async" width="30" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="75" data-file-height="100" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA#Rendering_issues" title="Help:IPA">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a>&#32;instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>Although there are many different dialects and accents, the transcription would be fairly standard.
</p>

<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Hallo! Hoe gaan dit?</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ɦalœu ɦu χɑːn dət]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Hallo! Hoe gaat het (met jou/je/u)?</i><br /><small>Also used: <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Hallo! Hoe is het?</i></i></small>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ɦɑloː ɦu ɣaːn ɦət]</span>
</td>
<td>Hello! How goes it? (Hello! How are you?)
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Hallo! Wie geht's?</i> (<i lang="de" title="German language text">Hallo! Wie geht's dir/Ihnen?</i>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Baie goed, dankie.</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[baiə χut daŋki]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Heel goed, dank je.</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ɦeːl ɣut dɑŋk jə]</span>
</td>
<td>Very well, thank you.
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Sehr gut, danke.</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Praat jy Afrikaans?</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[prɑːt jəi afrikɑːns]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Spreek/Praat jij/je Afrikaans?</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[spreːk/praːt jɛi̯/jə ɑfrikaːns]</span>
</td>
<td>Do you speak Afrikaans?
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Sprichst du Afrikaans?</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Praat jy Engels?</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[prɑːt jəi ɛŋəls]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Spreek/Praat jij/je Engels?</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[spreːk/praːt jɛi̯/jə ɛŋəls]</span>
</td>
<td>Do you speak English?
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Sprichst du Englisch?</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Ja.</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[jɑː]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Ja.</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[jaː]</span>
</td>
<td>Yes.
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Ja.</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Nee.</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[nɪə]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Nee.</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[neː]</span>
</td>
<td>No.
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Nein.</i><br /><small> Also: <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Nee.</i></i> (Colloquial)</small>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">'n Bietjie.</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ə biki]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Een beetje.</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ə beːtjə]</span>
</td>
<td>A bit.
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Ein bisschen.</i> Sometimes shortened in text: "'n bisschen"
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Wat is jou naam?</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[vat əs jœu nɑːm]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Hoe heet jij/je?</i> / <i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Wat is jouw naam?</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ʋɑt ɪs jɑu̯ naːm]</span>
</td>
<td>What is your name?
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Wie heißt du?</i> / <i lang="de" title="German language text">Wie ist dein Name?</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Die kinders praat Afrikaans.</i></b>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[di kənərs prɑːt afrikɑːns]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">De kinderen spreken/praten Afrikaans.</i>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[də kɪndərən spreːkən/praːtən ɑfrikaːns]</span>
</td>
<td>The children speak Afrikaans.
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Die Kinder sprechen Afrikaans.</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Ek is lief vir jou.</i></b><br /><small>Less common: <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">Ek het jou lief</i></i>. </small>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[æk əs lif fər jœu]</span>
</td>
<td><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Ik hou van jou/je.</i><br /><small>Common in Southern Dutch: <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Ik heb je/jou/u lief</i></i>.</small>
</td>
<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ɪk ɦɑu̯ vɑn jɑu̯/jə]</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ɪk ɦɛb jə/jɑu̯/y lif]</span>
</td>
<td>I love you.
</td>
<td><i lang="de" title="German language text">Ich liebe dich.</i><br /><small> Also: <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Ich habe dich lieb.</i></i> (Colloquial; virtually no romantic connotation) </small>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch language</a> the word <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Afrikaans</i></i> means African, in the general sense. Consequently, Afrikaans is commonly denoted as <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Zuid-Afrikaans</i></i>. This ambiguity also exists in Afrikaans itself and is either resolved in the context of its usage, or by using <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Afrikaner</i></i> for an <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Africa" title="Indigenous peoples of Africa">African person</a>, and <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch language text">Afrika-</i></i> in the adjective sense.
</p><p>A handful of Afrikaans words are exactly the same as in English. The following Afrikaans sentences, for example, are exactly the same in the two languages, in terms of both their meaning and spelling; only their pronunciation differs.
</p>
<ul><li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">My pen was in my hand.</i></b> (<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[məi pɛn vas ən məi ɦant]</span>)</li>
<li><b><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans language text">My hand is in warm water.</i></b> (<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[məi ɦant əs ən varm vɑːtər]</span>)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sample text">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Psalm_23" title="Psalm 23">Psalm 23</a> 1983 translation:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div style="margin-left: 1em; font-style: italic;" lang="af" class="poem">
<p>Die Here is my Herder, ek kom niks kort nie.<br />
Hy laat my in groen weivelde rus. Hy bring my by waters waar daar vrede is.<br />
Hy gee my nuwe krag. Hy lei my op die regte paaie tot eer van Sy naam.<br />
Selfs al gaan ek deur donker dieptes, sal ek nie bang wees nie, want U is by my. In U hande is ek veilig.
</p>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Psalm_23" title="Psalm 23">Psalm 23</a> alternative translation:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div style="margin-left: 1em; font-style: italic;" lang="af" class="poem">
<p>Die Here is my Herder, niks sal my ontbreek nie.<br />
Hy laat my neerlê in groen weivelde; na waters waar rus is, lei Hy my heen.<br />
Hy verkwik my siel; Hy lei my in die spore van geregtigheid, om sy Naam ontwil.<br />
Al gaan ek ook in 'n dal van doodskaduwee, ek sal geen onheil vrees nie; want U is met my: u stok en u staf die vertroos my.
</p>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Prayer" title="Lord&#39;s Prayer">Lord's Prayer</a> (Afrikaans New Living translation)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div style="margin-left: 1em; font-style: italic;" lang="af" class="poem">
<p>Ons Vader in die hemel, laat U Naam geheilig word.<br />
Laat U koningsheerskappy spoedig kom.<br />
Laat U wil hier op aarde uitgevoer word soos in die hemel.<br />
Gee ons die porsie brood wat ons vir vandag nodig het.<br />
En vergeef ons ons sondeskuld soos ons ook óns skuldenaars vergewe het.<br />
Bewaar ons sodat ons nie aan verleiding sal toegee nie; en bevry ons van die greep van die Bose.<br />
Want van U is die koninkryk,<br />
en die krag,<br />
en die heerlikheid,<br />
tot in ewigheid. Amen
</p>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Prayer" title="Lord&#39;s Prayer">Lord's Prayer</a> (Original translation):<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div style="margin-left: 1em; font-style: italic;" lang="af" class="poem">
<p>Onse Vader wat in die hemel is,<br />
laat U Naam geheilig word;<br />
laat U koninkryk kom;<br />
laat U wil geskied op die aarde,<br />
net soos in die hemel.<br />
Gee ons vandag ons daaglikse brood;<br />
en vergeef ons ons skulde<br />
soos ons ons skuldenaars vergewe<br />
en laat ons nie in die versoeking nie<br />
maar verlos ons van die Bose<br />
Want aan U behoort die koninkryk<br />
en die krag<br />
en die heerlikheid<br />
tot in ewigheid. Amen
</p>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afrikaans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Afrikaans borrowed from other languages such as Portuguese, German, Malay, Bantu and Khoisan languages; see <a href="#CITEREFSebba1997">Sebba 1997</a>, p.&#160;160, <a href="#CITEREFNieslerLouwRoux2005">Niesler, Louw &amp; Roux 2005</a>, p.&#160;459.<br />90 to 95% of Afrikaans vocabulary is ultimately of Dutch origin; see <a href="#CITEREFMesthrie1995">Mesthrie 1995</a>, p.&#160;214, <a href="#CITEREFMesthrie2002">Mesthrie 2002</a>, p.&#160;205, <a href="#CITEREFKamwangamalu2004">Kamwangamalu 2004</a>, p.&#160;203, <a href="#CITEREFBerdichevsky2004">Berdichevsky 2004</a>, p.&#160;131, <a href="#CITEREFBrachinVincent1985">Brachin &amp; Vincent 1985</a>, p.&#160;132.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For morphology; see <a href="#CITEREFHolm1989">Holm 1989</a>, p.&#160;338, <a href="#CITEREFGeertsClyne1992">Geerts &amp; Clyne 1992</a>, p.&#160;72. For grammar and spelling; see <a href="#CITEREFSebba1997">Sebba 1997</a>, p.&#160;161.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Dutch and Afrikaans share mutual intelligibility; see <a href="#CITEREFGooskens2007">Gooskens 2007</a>, p.&#160;453, <a href="#CITEREFHolm1989">Holm 1989</a>, p.&#160;338, <a href="#CITEREFBakerPrys_Jones1997">Baker &amp; Prys Jones 1997</a>, p.&#160;302, <a href="#CITEREFEgil_BreivikHåkon_Jahr1987">Egil Breivik &amp; Håkon Jahr 1987</a>, p.&#160;232.<br />For written mutual intelligibility; see <a href="#CITEREFSebba2007">Sebba 2007</a>, <a href="#CITEREFSebba1997">Sebba 1997</a>, p.&#160;161.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-speakers-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-speakers_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">What follows are estimations. Afrikaans has 16.3 million speakers; see <a href="#CITEREFde_Swaan2001">de Swaan 2001</a>, p.&#160;216. Afrikaans has a total of 16 million speakers; see <a href="#CITEREFMachan2009">Machan 2009</a>, p.&#160;174. About 9 million people speak Afrikaans as a second or third language; see <a href="#CITEREFAlant2004">Alant 2004</a>, p.&#160;45, <a href="#CITEREFProost2006">Proost 2006</a>, p.&#160;402. Afrikaans has over 5 million native speakers and 15 million second-language speakers; see <a href="#CITEREFRéguer2004">Réguer 2004</a>, p.&#160;20. Afrikaans has about 6 million native and 16 million second language speakers; see <a href="#CITEREFDomínguezLópez1995">Domínguez &amp; López 1995</a>, p.&#160;340. In South Africa, over 23 million people speak Afrikaans, of which a third are first-language speakers; see <a href="#CITEREFPageSonnenburg2003">Page &amp; Sonnenburg 2003</a>, p.&#160;7. L2 "Black Afrikaans" is spoken, with different degrees of fluency, by an estimated 15 million; see <a href="#CITEREFStell2008–2011">Stell 2008–2011</a>, p.&#160;1.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It has the widest geographical and racial distribution of all the official languages of South Africa; see <a href="#CITEREFWebb2003">Webb 2003</a>, pp.&#160;7, 8, <a href="#CITEREFBerdichevsky2004">Berdichevsky 2004</a>, p.&#160;131. It has by far the largest geographical distribution; see <a href="#CITEREFAlant2004">Alant 2004</a>, p.&#160;45.<br />It is widely spoken and understood as a second or third language; see <a href="#CITEREFDeumertVandenbussche2003">Deumert &amp; Vandenbussche 2003</a>, p.&#160;16, <a href="#CITEREFKamwangamalu2004">Kamwangamalu 2004</a>, p.&#160;207, <a href="#CITEREFMyers-Scotton2006">Myers-Scotton 2006</a>, p.&#160;389, <a href="#CITEREFSimpson2008">Simpson 2008</a>, p.&#160;324, <a href="#CITEREFPalmer2001">Palmer 2001</a>, p.&#160;141, <a href="#CITEREFWebb2002">Webb 2002</a>, p.&#160;74, <a href="#CITEREFHerrimanBurnaby1996">Herriman &amp; Burnaby 1996</a>, p.&#160;18, <a href="#CITEREFPageSonnenburg2003">Page &amp; Sonnenburg 2003</a>, p.&#160;7, <a href="#CITEREFBrook_Napier2007">Brook Napier 2007</a>, pp.&#160;69, 71.<br />An estimated 40% have at least a basic level of communication; see <a href="#CITEREFWebb2003">Webb 2003</a>, p.&#160;7 <a href="#CITEREFMcLeanMcCormick1996">McLean &amp; McCormick 1996</a>, p.&#160;333.</span>
</li>
</ol></div>

<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Afrikaans was historically called Cape Dutch; see <a href="#CITEREFDeumertVandenbussche2003">Deumert &amp; Vandenbussche 2003</a>, p.&#160;16, <a href="#CITEREFConradie2005">Conradie 2005</a>, p.&#160;208, <a href="#CITEREFSebba1997">Sebba 1997</a>, p.&#160;160, <a href="#CITEREFLangerDavies2005">Langer &amp; Davies 2005</a>, p.&#160;144, <a href="#CITEREFDeumert2002">Deumert 2002</a>, p.&#160;3, <a href="#CITEREFBerdichevsky2004">Berdichevsky 2004</a>, p.&#160;130.<br />Afrikaans is rooted in seventeenth century dialects of Dutch; see <a href="#CITEREFHolm1989">Holm 1989</a>, p.&#160;338, <a href="#CITEREFGeertsClyne1992">Geerts &amp; Clyne 1992</a>, p.&#160;71, <a href="#CITEREFMesthrie1995">Mesthrie 1995</a>, p.&#160;214, <a href="#CITEREFNieslerLouwRoux2005">Niesler, Louw &amp; Roux 2005</a>, p.&#160;459.<br />Afrikaans is variously described as a <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a>, a partially creolised language, or a deviant variety of Dutch; see <a href="#CITEREFSebba2007">Sebba 2007</a>, p.&#160;116.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">They were named before the establishment of the current <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape" title="Eastern Cape">Eastern Cape</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cape" title="Northern Cape">Northern Cape</a> provinces, and are not dialects of those provinces <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">per se</i></i>.</span>
</li>
